  29. Only two shaves into this Braun, but think that's enough time for some early comments. By way of hirsute background . . . have been shaving for over five decades now and have owned a number of shavers, electric and safety. Still, have found myself locked into blade-shaving for about the past 5 years. That's because since retirement, I've lately been getting lazy about taking the time for the daily ritual of a good, complete blade shave. But the wife let me know more than once that she didn't appreciate smoozing against a 2 or 3 day growth of sharp, facial hair. So, about 2 years ago I bought a Panasonic shaver that took accolades from Consumer Reports. I gave it a fair trial, but after breaking in my face to an electric shaver, I found I was spending an inordinate amount of time \\"rowing\\" the Panasonic back and forth across my moderate growth, just to get a reasonable shave . . . never mind a \\"good\\" one. So, I went back to my non-daily blade shave routine, suffering the wife's adversity to close-up contact on my hairier days.<br /> But still, I wanted to give electric shavers another whack, so -- skipping CR reviews this time -- I started researching both the foil & rotary offerings. An early case of sticker shock pretty much told me I would be condemned to return to a blade-shave if I couldn't locate a winner at a moderate price. It almost came down to a coin flip between offerings from Norelco and Braun. The deciding factor was I remembered being happy with a couple of Braun's from years back, and unhappy with my one rotary shaver purchase, several decades ago. So, Braun it was.<br /> Thirty seconds into my first shave, I wondered why some users had complained about the noise. Yes, I'm sure it's louder than a rotary, but it's also much more quite than the highly rated Panasonic I'd put out to pasture, and definitely doesn't assault my ear drums like I'd expected, based on some reviews. I did take the trouble to set-up my first shave with a pre-shave lotion (Lectric Shave), so that likely helped out a bit. But, without exaggeration, I was very, very happy with the results. Not only did I walk away with a baby-butt smooth face, but it hadn't taken that much time or swipes across the face to do it. Also, it cleanly took out a hairy trouble patch on the neck that I'd always had to attack with a blade from 3 or 4 different angles. While I'm happy I chose a shaver that can be quickly rinse-cleaned under tap water, I'm equally glad I skipped the higher price of a \\"total soak\\" model, frankly because I'm just not a big fan of shower shaving. (I always thought a guy has enough to do in a shower, without worrying about drop-smashing expensive electronics!) Haven't yet gotten into stuff like, # of shaves per charge, side trimmer effectiveness or any of that. But unlike the first few shaves on my last electric, I am genuinely happy with this puppy and would suggest anyone wanting a truly good, close shave -- if willing to skip the more costly bells & whistles of other models -- will not be disappointed. Enjoy!

They shave perfect without having to \\"scrub\\" and without nicks and burning. Now the new style is even better. Previously, the \\"blades\\" were vertical, rubbing against a horizontal screen. This is the way ALL screen shavers shaved. The new ones have a horizontal sheet sliding back and forth against a horizontal screen. It works better than the vertical blades. It's also easier to clean. The vertical blades required physical brushing to get rid of the whisker-mulch... hot water alone wouldn't clean them. The new heads drop the \\"mulch\\" into the bottom of the head and there is nothing to gum-up like the vertical blades. A rinse under the faucet cleans it entirely, even without taking the head off. It's a perfect design from an engineering standpoint.

  124. I have had this razor for a year now and am very satisfied with its performance. It replaced a Braun 8595 (which died) _and_ a Norelco 905RX. The reason it replaced both razors is that I had to use them both to get a good shave. The Braun shaved close, but didn't seem to do as well on non-flat areas (like the neck) or with longer hairs. The Norelco did fine on these difficult areas, but just wasn't that close of a shave. The 320-S4 does what each these prior razors did best - shaves close and shaves well in all areas while handling longer hairs.<br />The prior Braun was their highest-end model and used a cleaning system. The cleaning system worked fine, but it was quite expensive paying for the solution that had to be replaced frequently. After about 3 years or so, the cleaning system stopped working, which actually was fine, because it really was a bit of overkill. Not requiring a cleaning system for this razor is good. And being able to just clean it with water is a plus (couldn't do that with the 8595).<br />Another good thing about this razor is that it can run using the electric cord, in case the battery runs out. Couldn't do that with the prior Braun. And it seems to charge up fairly quickly, as well.<br />A couple negatives, though. The replacement head (foil and blade) costs about 45% of what was paid for the complete razor. The other negative is that the battery seems to hold about 20-30% less charge than when it was new. (I run the razor longer than normal, since I also shave my entire head daily. So my 1 year of use probably compares to what most folks would use in 1 1/2 or 2.) It's possible this might have resulted from recharging the razor as soon as the low-battery light came on. I have since discovered that the warning light comes on with about 10 minutes of charge left, so I am now using it until it stops and then finishing while plugged in.<br /><br />Pros<br />1) Shaves all contours well<br />2) Can handle longer hairs (withouthaving to use trimmer)<br />3) Can be rinse-cleaned with water<br />4) Charges up quickly<br />5) Can run on power cord when discharged<br />6) Great price point<br /><br />Cons<br />1) Cost of replacement cutters<br />2) Possible battery life issue<br /><br />Bottom line - I'd buy this razor again if I needed a new one.

Took it to Interstate batteries who can generally change rechargeable batteries in just about anything, but they said due to the closed nature of this system (being able to submerse in water to clean the head) they can't access and change the battery.<br /><br />So it was time to trash it, and after that impressive time frame, and the fact that it gives a much closer shave than rotaries, there was no doubt that I would replace it with another Braun in the low price end of their line up. Done.<br /><br />Took my first shave with it yesterday and it is smooth as glass, sliding over the face. Although I must admit that I topped off the shave with a single dry stroke of a double blade razor against the grain, to get the glass smooth finish on my skin. By the way, the it is best to shave with the Braun, before hitting the shower or cleaning the face. That is recommended by Braun, probaby because the oils on your skin, kind of lubricate the skin surface and the stiffer whiskers tend to stand up better for the screen and cutters to catch them, than they do when softened in the shower.<br /><br />Only negative on this model is no hard clamshell style case like my earlier Braun to protect it in transit. But the same snap on guard on my first Braun, clipped over the sides of the head and in fairly short order failed (one of the snap edges cracked through stress of use, rendering the guard inoperable) so I was glad I had the hard case for suitcase and travel, because the micro screen that catches whiskers and protects the skin from blade abrasion, is by nature and design, very thin and delicate. Hitting it against anything will chip a hole in the screen and make it useless. And that was the cause of 3 or 4 screen replacements over 10 years, so I learned to be very careful with the screen.<br /><br />It is a good idea when purchasing a Braun, to always have a backup screen and blade set for those unpredictable moments.   320. This thing works great. Close, comfortable, excellent shave. I've only had it for a few weeks, but it's clear it's a great item. My beard is full but fine (meaning not particularly course). This shaver took care of six days' growth with no problem. On a coarser beard it might only cut it (pun intended) for three/four days' worth. We'll have to see how long it lasts, though. I say that because this is the fourth Braun foil shaver I've owned... and each has had a shorter lifespan than the one before it. Granted, the first one was from 1987 or '88. Wish I could remember what that model was called. It was old-school Braun: simple foil (one) that was rounded across the top and didn't move or flex to follow your face, cutter block beneath. Had the pop-up trimmer also (I guess they all do). Came with a nice case that had little fitted spaces inside for the shaver and the folded-up cord. One side of the case had a mirror mounted in it. It was about $80 (1987 or '88 dollars, of course). The outside of the unit was actually thin metal (appeared to be brushed aluminum) and had rubber grippy dots on the lower two-thirds. \\"Made in Germany\\" prominently noted upon it under the top third that snaps off (where the cutter block resides). It worked really well and lasted for I think 13 years. Made two trips to an appliance-service joint to have the battery replaced during that time. I am sharing all this only as illustration that NOTHING is made like it used to be. Such a shame. Yet we all have little choice but to accommodate it as best we can. So, the motor on that one finally died, like I said, after quite a long time. Braun still made the same thing, only in a \\"newer\\" version (i.e., more cheaply made and not quite as nice). It was essentially the same thing, although now all black plastic. No more metal outer skin or rubbery grippy dots, still came with a fitted case (no more mirror though). Still made in Germany anyway, about the same price as the first one (though I guess actually more, given inflation). After about eight years and one battery change, it died as well. At this point I was told by two different appliance-repair joints that the battery is no longer available or even replaceable; the motor and battery are a single unit in the current models. \\"What can I do?\\" I asked. \\"Nothing,\\" was the answer. \\"You just have to buy a whole new shaver.\\" Great. Third one was where Braun started making everything both MORE cheaply and MORE complicated. Excellent! Not. This is the one that bit it about a month ago. It lasted five years, tops. Cost about $100 at Target, seemed to be a middle-range unit. Can't recall what the model was, but it introduced the \\"dual floating foils with longer-hair trimmer in between\\" scene. Fine, fine. Didn't seem to work any better than the earlier, single non-moving foil. Plus replacement foils/blocks were awfully pricey (about $30, whereas foil and block for each of the older ones were less than half that). The case was now a formless and cheesy zippered pouch (still on hand though, with a pair of small binoculars in it). Anyway, again, good-performing item, no doubt. One day it refused to shut off, though. Somehow or other the switch had broken. No amount of gentle anything would turn it off. At length I tried pushing the power button with the corner of the counter in my bathroom. This ended up just breaking it completely. But at least it was off. Into the trash it went. So, given how each Braun shaver I've owned has lasted LESS time... I figured there was no good reason to go with any of the models above this one. Those $200 ones with the cleaner-tank thing? Why on earth? I have a friend who owns one of those; he's convinced that the high-tech cleaner tank doesn't do anything to justify its price. I think there are some that are even more expensive. I chose the 320-S based on a few things: It's washable (though a good blowing out after each use and that plus using the little brush every few uses seems fine, just as with the older ones). It'll work corded or cordless, so if you run out of battery after doing half your face you don't have to wait around for a bit charging (not all Brauns will work corded, and why that is is a huge mystery), the power cord adjusts to international voltages by itself (not that I spend a lot of time out of the country, but this will be useful at some point I bet). Doesn't come with a case at all (need to go up a few models for that). And as some others have noted, the weird and elaborate plastoid \\"cap\\" thingie is junk. Look at it the wrong way and it will fall off. One thing that was frustrating was the amount of time I had to spend on the Braun website, figuring out that not all models have the same features here. It should be easier than it was to figure out. Bottom line (finally): This shaver works great, and unless you're into pricey things for their own sake there seems to be very little reason to spend any more on one of the higher models, especially in that these don't seem to last as long as they did a bunch of years ago (but then, what does). The only exception I can think of is if you prefer to use it wet (this one doesn't do that). The 320-S says \\"Made in China\\" under where the pop-up trimmer slides out. Well, not everything from China is junky, necessarily, but it's still another good reason to assume that this one will not last as long as the others... each of which died sooner, after all. So we'll see.

  464. I used Norelco shavers for all my life before switching to the Braun. The Braun gives a much closer shave, faster, with less irritation, at a much cheaper price. The Braun chews hair off your face with a few strokes and can handle longer scruff way more effectively. I have a very angular face, and irregular facial hair pattern and growth. I do not have thick, full facial hair. Rather sharp and dispersed facial hair.<br /><br />For me. the hardest shaving point is my neck. The Norelcos NEVER shaved that hair even with repeat strokes, different angles, different grips, and varied pressure. However, they would succeed at chaffing and irritating the skin quite well. The ONLY way the Norelcos would shave my neck hair was if I used the pop out trimmer and tediously and skillfully attacked small patches of hair and then went over with the circular blades once the hair was short enough, and even then the shave was mediocre at best. The Braun, removes much more neck hair, much faster, with significantly less irritation. It doesn't magically remove ALL the neck hair. I still have to target a few difficult hairs with the pop out trimmer to make them short enough before the shaver will get them. The pop out trimmer on the Braun lacks trimming power, which is why I gave the Braun 4 stars and not 5.<br /><br />Another HUGE plus for the Braun, is that you can use the shaver while it is plugged into a power source. This may sound trivial, but it is actually quite important. If your shaver discharges mid shave, you simply plug the Braun in and finish the job. The Norelco lithium battery shaver I had, would NOT function while it was charging. So, if you only got through half your shave before discharge, sorry but you will have to wait an hour before you have enough charge to finish the job. What's that? Its 10PM and you want to go to bed for work tomorrow? Excuse me? Its 7AM and you have half a shave and you need to catch your 730AM bus? Sorry you're out luck buddy. Enjoy going to work with half your facial hair. I really hope Norelco fixed that problem.<br /><br />The Braun's battery is strong and the shaver functions with an equal amount of power whether its plugged into the wall or its functioning on battery. Again, this my sound trivial, but it is actually VERY important. You want an electric shaver to rotate as quickly as possible because that gives it shaving power which translates to less strokes, faster shave, and less irritation. The Norelcos I used in the past that COULD shave while plugged into the outlet, would have maximum shaving power while plugged in, but as soon as the cord was removed and the shaver switched over to battery, the Norelco would drop power and function with 10-20% less gusto.<br /><br />Overall, I am very pleased with the Braun. Its nice to finish off a shave, and not have super chaffed and irritated skin. I can shave with the Braun in the morning and not suffer significant chaffing or irritation, and then go about the rest of my day feeling good about my skin. I would NEVER, attempt that with a Norelco. A Norelco shave always had to be be a night affair for me, so that my skin had the night to recover from the chaffing.<br /><br />I bought this introduction level shaver because I was not sure if the Braun would be effective and I didn't want to spend alot of money finding out. After my experience with this Braun, I have no hesitation about purchasing this shaver or one of their higher level, more expensive shavers in the future.
